			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Climate change mitigation</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>

Global mean surface temperature change from 1880 to 2016, relative to the 1951–1980 mean. The black line is the global annual mean and the red line is the five-year <a href="/wiki/Local_regression" title="Local regression">lowess smooth</a>. The blue <a href="/wiki/Error_bar" title="Error bar">uncertainty bars</a> show a 95% confidence limit. Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://data.giss.nasa.gov/gistemp/">NASA GISS</a>. <a href="/wiki/Global_dimming" title="Global dimming">Global dimming</a>, from <a href="/wiki/Sulfate_aerosol" title="Sulfate aerosol">sulfate aerosol</a> air pollution, between 1950 and 1980 is believed to have mitigated global warming somewhat.</div>

<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Global_public_support_for_energy_sources_(Ipsos_2011).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Global public support for energy sources, based on a survey by Ipsos (2011).<sup id="cite_ref-ipsos_2011_preference_for_renewables_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipsos_2011_preference_for_renewables-2">[2]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Climate change mitigation</b> consists of actions to limit the magnitude or rate of long-term <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">climate change</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Climate change mitigation generally involves reductions in human (<a href="/wiki/Anthropogenic" class="mw-redirect" title="Anthropogenic">anthropogenic</a>) emissions of <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gases</a> (GHGs).<sup id="cite_ref-ipcc_mitigation_options_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipcc_mitigation_options-4">[4]</a></sup> Mitigation may also be achieved by increasing the capacity of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_sink" title="Carbon sink">carbon sinks</a>, e.g., through <a href="/wiki/Reforestation" title="Reforestation">reforestation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ipcc_mitigation_options_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipcc_mitigation_options-4">[4]</a></sup> Mitigation policies can substantially reduce the risks associated with human-induced global warming.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Panel_on_Climate_Change" class="mw-redirect" title="International Panel on Climate Change">IPCC's</a> 2014 <a href="/wiki/IPCC_Fifth_Assessment_Report" title="IPCC Fifth Assessment Report">assessment report</a>, "Mitigation is a public good; climate change is a case of the '<a href="/wiki/Tragedy_of_the_commons" title="Tragedy of the commons">tragedy of the commons</a>. Effective climate change mitigation will not be achieved if each agent (individual, institution or country) acts independently in its own selfish interest (See <a href="/wiki/International_cooperation" class="mw-redirect" title="International cooperation">International cooperation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emissions_trading" title="Emissions trading">Emissions trading</a>), suggesting the need for collective action. Some adaptation actions, on the other hand, have characteristics of a private good as benefits of actions may accrue more directly to the individuals, regions, or countries that undertake them, at least in the short term. Nevertheless, financing such adaptive activities remains an issue, particularly for poor individuals and countries."<sup id="cite_ref-AR5-WG3-Chap3_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR5-WG3-Chap3-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Examples of mitigation include <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_phase-out" title="Fossil fuel phase-out">phasing out fossil fuels</a> by switching to <a href="/wiki/Low-carbon_power" title="Low-carbon power">low-carbon energy</a> sources, such as <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear energy</a>, and expanding forests and other "sinks" to remove greater amounts of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_in_Earth%27s_atmosphere" title="Carbon dioxide in Earth's atmosphere">carbon dioxide</a> from the atmosphere.<sup id="cite_ref-ipcc_mitigation_options_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipcc_mitigation_options-4">[4]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Efficient_energy_use" title="Efficient energy use">Energy efficiency</a> may also play a role,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> for example, through improving the <a href="/wiki/Building_insulation" title="Building insulation">insulation of buildings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Another approach to climate change mitigation is <a href="/wiki/Climate_engineering" title="Climate engineering">climate engineering</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most countries are parties to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Framework_Convention_on_Climate_Change" title="United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change">United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change</a> (UNFCCC).<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The ultimate objective of the UNFCCC is to stabilize atmospheric concentrations of GHGs at a level that would prevent dangerous human interference of the climate system.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Scientific analysis can provide information on the impacts of climate change, but deciding which impacts are dangerous requires value judgments.<sup id="cite_ref-wg_2_ch19_dangerous_climate_change_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wg_2_ch19_dangerous_climate_change-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, Parties to the UNFCCC agreed that future global warming should be limited to below 2.0&#160;°C (3.6&#160;°F) relative to the pre-<a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">industrial</a> level.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> With the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Agreement" title="Paris Agreement">Paris Agreement</a> of 2015 this was confirmed, but was revised with a new target laying down "parties will do the best" to achieve warming below 1.5&#160;°C.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-14">[14]</a></sup> The current trajectory of global greenhouse gas emissions does not appear to be consistent with limiting global warming to below 1.5 or 2&#160;°C.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Other mitigation policies have been proposed, some of which are more stringent<sup id="cite_ref-existing_policies_inadequate_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-existing_policies_inadequate-16">[16]</a></sup> or modest<sup id="cite_ref-van_vuuren_mitigation_policy_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-van_vuuren_mitigation_policy-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nordhaus_2010_cba_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nordhaus_2010_cba-18">[18]</a></sup> than the 2&#160;°C limit.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Greenhouse_gas_concentrations_and_stabilization">Greenhouse gas concentrations and stabilization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_mitigation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Greenhouse gas concentrations and stabilization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas#Removal_from_the_atmosphere_and_global_warming_potential" title="Greenhouse gas">Greenhouse gas §&#160;Removal from the atmosphere and global warming potential</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:324px;max-width:324px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:322px;max-width:322px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Stabilizing_carbon_dioxide_emissions_at_their_present_level_will_not_stabilize_its_concentration_in_the_atmosphere.png" class="image"><img alt="refer to caption and adjacent text" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Stabilizing_carbon_dioxide_emissions_at_their_present_level_will_not_stabilize_its_concentration_in_the_atmosphere.png/320px-Stabilizing_carbon_dioxide_emissions_at_their_present_level_will_not_stabilize_its_concentration_in_the_atmosphere.png" width="320" height="116" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Stabilizing_carbon_dioxide_emissions_at_their_present_level_will_not_stabilize_its_concentration_in_the_atmosphere.png/480px-Stabilizing_carbon_dioxide_emissions_at_their_present_level_will_not_stabilize_its_concentration_in_the_atmosphere.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Stabilizing_carbon_dioxide_emissions_at_their_present_level_will_not_stabilize_its_concentration_in_the_atmosphere.png/640px-Stabilizing_carbon_dioxide_emissions_at_their_present_level_will_not_stabilize_its_concentration_in_the_atmosphere.png 2x" data-file-width="1436" data-file-height="519" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Stabilizing CO<sub>2</sub> emissions at their present level would not stabilize its concentration in the atmosphere.<sup id="cite_ref-meehl_stabilizing_ghg_concentrations_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meehl_stabilizing_ghg_concentrations-19">[19]</a></sup></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:322px;max-width:322px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Stabilizing_the_atmospheric_concentration_of_carbon_dioxide_at_a_constant_level_would_require_emissions_to_be_effectively_eliminated.png" class="image"><img alt="refer to caption and adjacent text" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Stabilizing_the_atmospheric_concentration_of_carbon_dioxide_at_a_constant_level_would_require_emissions_to_be_effectively_eliminated.png/320px-Stabilizing_the_atmospheric_concentration_of_carbon_dioxide_at_a_constant_level_would_require_emissions_to_be_effectively_eliminated.png" width="320" height="116" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Stabilizing_the_atmospheric_concentration_of_carbon_dioxide_at_a_constant_level_would_require_emissions_to_be_effectively_eliminated.png/480px-Stabilizing_the_atmospheric_concentration_of_carbon_dioxide_at_a_constant_level_would_require_emissions_to_be_effectively_eliminated.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Stabilizing_the_atmospheric_concentration_of_carbon_dioxide_at_a_constant_level_would_require_emissions_to_be_effectively_eliminated.png/640px-Stabilizing_the_atmospheric_concentration_of_carbon_dioxide_at_a_constant_level_would_require_emissions_to_be_effectively_eliminated.png 2x" data-file-width="1436" data-file-height="520" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Stabilizing the atmospheric concentration of CO<sub>2</sub> at a constant level would require emissions to be effectively eliminated.<sup id="cite_ref-meehl_stabilizing_ghg_concentrations_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meehl_stabilizing_ghg_concentrations-19">[19]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>One of the issues often discussed in relation to climate change mitigation is the stabilization of greenhouse gas concentrations in the atmosphere. The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Framework_Convention_on_Climate_Change" title="United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change">United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change</a> (UNFCCC) has the ultimate objective of <a href="/wiki/Avoiding_dangerous_climate_change" class="mw-redirect" title="Avoiding dangerous climate change">preventing "dangerous" anthropogenic (i.e., human) interference of the climate system</a>. As is stated in Article 2 of the Convention, this requires that greenhouse gas (GHG) concentrations are stabilized in the atmosphere at a level where <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_and_ecosystems" title="Climate change and ecosystems">ecosystems</a> can adapt naturally to climate change, <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_and_agriculture" title="Climate change and agriculture">food production</a> is not threatened, and <a href="/wiki/Economics_of_global_warming" title="Economics of global warming">economic development</a> can proceed in a sustainable fashion.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are a number of anthropogenic greenhouse gases. These include <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a> (<a href="/wiki/Chemical_formula" title="Chemical formula">chemical formula</a>: CO<sub>2</sub>), <a href="/wiki/Methane" title="Methane">methane</a> (<span class="chemf nowrap">CH<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><br />
4</span></span>), <a href="/wiki/Nitrous_oxide" title="Nitrous oxide">nitrous oxide</a> (<span class="chemf nowrap">N<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><br />
2</span>O</span>), and a group of gases referred to as <a href="/wiki/Halocarbon" title="Halocarbon">halocarbons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The emissions reductions necessary to stabilize the atmospheric concentrations of these gases varies.<sup id="cite_ref-meehl_stabilizing_ghg_concentrations_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meehl_stabilizing_ghg_concentrations-19">[19]</a></sup> CO<sub>2</sub> is the most important of the anthropogenic greenhouse gases (see <a href="/wiki/Radiative_forcing" title="Radiative forcing">radiative forcing</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>There is a difference between stabilizing CO<sub>2</sub> emissions and stabilizing atmospheric concentrations of CO<sub>2</sub>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Stabilizing emissions of CO<sub>2</sub> at current levels would not lead to a stabilization in the atmospheric concentration of CO<sub>2</sub>. In fact, stabilizing emissions at current levels would result in the atmospheric concentration of CO<sub>2</sub> continuing to rise over the 21st century and beyond (see the graphs opposite).</p>
<p>The reason for this is that human activities are adding CO<sub>2</sub> to the atmosphere far faster than natural processes can remove it (see <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_in_Earth%27s_atmosphere" title="Carbon dioxide in Earth's atmosphere">carbon dioxide in Earth's atmosphere</a> for a complete explanation).<sup id="cite_ref-meehl_stabilizing_ghg_concentrations_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meehl_stabilizing_ghg_concentrations-19">[19]</a></sup> This is analogous to a flow of water into a bathtub.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> So long as the tap runs water (analogous to the emission of carbon dioxide) into the tub faster than water escapes through the plughole (the natural removal of carbon dioxide from the atmosphere), then the level of water in the tub (analogous to the concentration of carbon dioxide in the atmosphere) will continue to rise.</p>
<p>According to some studies, stabilizing atmospheric CO<sub>2</sub> concentrations would require anthropogenic CO<sub>2</sub> emissions to be reduced by 80% relative to the peak emissions level.<sup id="cite_ref-us_nrc_co2_stabilization_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-us_nrc_co2_stabilization-25">[25]</a></sup> An 80% reduction in emissions would stabilize CO<sub>2</sub> concentrations for around a century, but even greater reductions would be required beyond this.<sup id="cite_ref-meehl_stabilizing_ghg_concentrations_19-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meehl_stabilizing_ghg_concentrations-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-us_nrc_co2_stabilization_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-us_nrc_co2_stabilization-25">[25]</a></sup> Other research has found that, after leaving room for emissions for food production for 9 billion people and to keep the global temperature rise below 2&#160;°C, emissions from energy production and transport will have to peak almost immediately in the developed world and decline at ca. 10% per annum until zero emissions are reached around 2030. In developing countries energy and transport emissions would have to peak by 2025 and then decline similarly.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>Stabilizing the atmospheric concentration of the other greenhouse gasses humans emit also depends on how fast their emissions are added to the atmosphere, and how fast the GHGs are removed. Stabilization for these gases is described in the later section on <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_mitigation#Non-CO2_greenhouse_gases" title="Climate change mitigation">non-CO<sub>2</sub> GHGs</a>.</p>
<dl>
<dt>Projections</dt>
</dl>
<p>Projections of future greenhouse gas emissions are highly uncertain.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> In the absence of policies to mitigate climate change, GHG emissions could rise significantly over the 21st century.<sup id="cite_ref-rogner_article_2_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rogner_article_2-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>Numerous assessments have considered how atmospheric GHG concentrations could be stabilized.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> The lower the desired stabilization level, the sooner global GHG emissions must peak and decline.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> GHG concentrations are unlikely to stabilize this century without major policy changes.<sup id="cite_ref-rogner_article_2_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rogner_article_2-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<table>
<tr>
<td>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Projected_carbon_dioxide_emissions_and_atmospheric_concentrations_over_the_21st_century_for_reference_and_mitigation_scenarios.png" class="image"><img alt="refer to caption and adjacent text" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Projected_carbon_dioxide_emissions_and_atmospheric_concentrations_over_the_21st_century_for_reference_and_mitigation_scenarios.png/320px-Projected_carbon_dioxide_emissions_and_atmospheric_concentrations_over_the_21st_century_for_reference_and_mitigation_scenarios.png" width="320" height="355" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Projected_carbon_dioxide_emissions_and_atmospheric_concentrations_over_the_21st_century_for_reference_and_mitigation_scenarios.png/480px-Projected_carbon_dioxide_emissions_and_atmospheric_concentrations_over_the_21st_century_for_reference_and_mitigation_scenarios.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Projected_carbon_dioxide_emissions_and_atmospheric_concentrations_over_the_21st_century_for_reference_and_mitigation_scenarios.png/640px-Projected_carbon_dioxide_emissions_and_atmospheric_concentrations_over_the_21st_century_for_reference_and_mitigation_scenarios.png 2x" data-file-width="1463" data-file-height="1621" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Projected_carbon_dioxide_emissions_and_atmospheric_concentrations_over_the_21st_century_for_reference_and_mitigation_scenarios.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Projected carbon dioxide emissions and atmospheric concentrations over the 21st century for reference and mitigation scenarios.</div>
</div>
</div>
</td>
<td>
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:335px;"><a href="/wiki/File:World_energy_consumption.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/World_energy_consumption.svg/333px-World_energy_consumption.svg.png" width="333" height="231" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/World_energy_consumption.svg/500px-World_energy_consumption.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/World_energy_consumption.svg/666px-World_energy_consumption.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="520" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:World_energy_consumption.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rate of world energy usage per day, from 1970 to 2010. Every fossil fuel source has increased in large amounts between 1970 and 2010, dominating all other energy sources. Hydroelectricity has increased at a slow steady rate over this same period, nuclear entered a period of rapid growth between 1970 and 1990 before leveling off. Other Renewables, between 2000 and 2010 have, having started from a low usage rate, began to enter into a period of rapid growth. 1000<a href="/wiki/TWh" class="mw-redirect" title="TWh">TWh</a>=1PWh.<sup id="cite_ref-BP-Report-2012_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BP-Report-2012-34">[34]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_consumption_by_power_source">Energy consumption by power source</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_mitigation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Energy consumption by power source">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Greenhouse_Gas_Emissions_from_Electricity_Production_IEA.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Greenhouse_Gas_Emissions_from_Electricity_Production_IEA.PNG/220px-Greenhouse_Gas_Emissions_from_Electricity_Production_IEA.PNG" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Greenhouse_Gas_Emissions_from_Electricity_Production_IEA.PNG/330px-Greenhouse_Gas_Emissions_from_Electricity_Production_IEA.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Greenhouse_Gas_Emissions_from_Electricity_Production_IEA.PNG/440px-Greenhouse_Gas_Emissions_from_Electricity_Production_IEA.PNG 2x" data-file-width="862" data-file-height="528" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Greenhouse_Gas_Emissions_from_Electricity_Production_IEA.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
"Hydropower-Internalised Costs and Externalised Benefits"; Frans H. Koch; <a href="/wiki/International_Energy_Agency" title="International Energy Agency">International Energy Agency</a> (IEA)-Implementing Agreement for Hydropower Technologies and Programmes; 2000.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>To create lasting climate change mitigation, the replacement of high carbon <a href="/wiki/Emission_intensity" title="Emission intensity">emission intensity</a> power sources, such as conventional <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a>—<a href="/wiki/Oil" title="Oil">oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>—with <a href="/wiki/Low-carbon_power" title="Low-carbon power">low-carbon power</a> sources is required. Fossil fuels supply humanity with the vast majority of our energy demands, and at a growing rate. In 2012 the IEA noted that coal accounted for half the increased energy use of the prior decade, growing faster than all renewable energy sources.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Both <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectricity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear power</a> together provide the majority of the generated <a href="/wiki/Low-carbon_power" title="Low-carbon power">low-carbon power</a> fraction of global total power consumption.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Methods_and_means">Methods and means</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_mitigation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Methods and means">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Emission_intensity" title="Emission intensity">Emission intensity</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Projected_global_primary_electricity_consumption_by_source,_over_the_21st_century,_for_a_climate_change_mitigation_scenario.png" class="image"><img alt="Refer to caption and image description" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Projected_global_primary_electricity_consumption_by_source%2C_over_the_21st_century%2C_for_a_climate_change_mitigation_scenario.png/220px-Projected_global_primary_electricity_consumption_by_source%2C_over_the_21st_century%2C_for_a_climate_change_mitigation_scenario.png" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Projected_global_primary_electricity_consumption_by_source%2C_over_the_21st_century%2C_for_a_climate_change_mitigation_scenario.png/330px-Projected_global_primary_electricity_consumption_by_source%2C_over_the_21st_century%2C_for_a_climate_change_mitigation_scenario.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Projected_global_primary_electricity_consumption_by_source%2C_over_the_21st_century%2C_for_a_climate_change_mitigation_scenario.png/440px-Projected_global_primary_electricity_consumption_by_source%2C_over_the_21st_century%2C_for_a_climate_change_mitigation_scenario.png 2x" data-file-width="1508" data-file-height="850" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Projected_global_primary_electricity_consumption_by_source,_over_the_21st_century,_for_a_climate_change_mitigation_scenario.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
This graph shows the projected contribution of various energy sources to world primary electricity consumption (PEC).<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> It is based on a climate change mitigation scenario, in which GHG emissions are substantially reduced over the 21st century. In the scenario, emission reductions are achieved using a portfolio of energy sources, as well as reductions in energy demand. <i>Also available in <a href="/wiki/File:Projected_global_primary_electricity_consumption_by_source,_over_the_21st_century,_for_a_climate_change_mitigation_scenario_(greyscale).png" title="File:Projected global primary electricity consumption by source, over the 21st century, for a climate change mitigation scenario (greyscale).png">greyscale</a>.</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Assessments often suggest that GHG emissions can be reduced using a portfolio of low-carbon technologies.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> At the core of most proposals is the reduction of <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> (GHG) emissions through reducing energy waste and switching to <a href="/wiki/Low-carbon_power" title="Low-carbon power">low-carbon power</a> sources of energy. As the cost of reducing GHG emissions in the <a href="/wiki/Electricity" title="Electricity">electricity</a> sector appears to be lower than in other sectors, such as in the <a href="/wiki/Transportation" class="mw-redirect" title="Transportation">transportation</a> sector, the electricity sector may deliver the largest proportional carbon reductions under an economically efficient climate policy.<sup id="cite_ref-issues_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-issues-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Economic tools can be useful in designing climate change mitigation policies." "While the limitations of economics and social welfare analysis, including cost–benefit analysis, are widely documented, economics nevertheless provides useful tools for assessing the pros and cons of taking, or not taking, action on climate change mitigation, as well as of adaptation measures, in achieving competing societal goals. Understanding these pros and cons can help in making policy decisions on climate change mitigation and can influence the actions taken by countries, institutions and individuals."<sup id="cite_ref-AR5-WG3-Chap3_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR5-WG3-Chap3-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other frequently discussed means include <a href="/wiki/Energy_conservation" title="Energy conservation">energy conservation</a>, increasing <a href="/wiki/Fuel_economy_in_automobiles" title="Fuel economy in automobiles">fuel economy in automobiles</a> (which includes the use of <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicle" title="Hybrid vehicle">electric hybrids</a>), charging <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrids</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">electric cars</a> by <a href="/wiki/Low-carbon_power" title="Low-carbon power">low-carbon electricity</a>, making <a href="/wiki/Individual_and_political_action_on_climate_change" title="Individual and political action on climate change">individual-lifestyle changes</a><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">cycling</a> instead of <a href="/wiki/Driving" title="Driving">driving</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Business_action_on_climate_change" title="Business action on climate change">changing business practices</a>. Many fossil fuel driven vehicles can be converted to use electricity, the U.S. has the potential to supply electricity for 73% of light duty vehicles (LDV), using overnight charging. The US average CO2 emissions for a battery-electric car is 180 grams per mile vs 430 grams per mile for a gasoline car.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The emissions would be displaced away from street level, where they have "high human-health implications. Increased use of electricity "generation for meeting the future transportation load is primarily fossil-fuel based", mostly natural gas, followed by coal,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> but could also be met through nuclear, tidal, hydroelectric and other sources.</p>
<p>A range of energy technologies may contribute to climate change mitigation.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> These include <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear power</a> and <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> sources such as <a href="/wiki/Biomass_preprocessing" class="mw-redirect" title="Biomass preprocessing">biomass</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectricity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind power</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar power</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_power" title="Geothermal power">geothermal power</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ocean_energy" class="mw-redirect" title="Ocean energy">ocean energy</a>, and; the use of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_sink" title="Carbon sink">carbon sinks</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Carbon_capture_and_storage" title="Carbon capture and storage">carbon capture and storage</a>. For example, Pacala and Socolow of Princeton<sup id="cite_ref-pacala2004sws_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pacala2004sws-46">[46]</a></sup> have proposed a 15 part program to reduce CO<sub>2</sub> emissions by 1 billion metric tons per year − or 25 billion tons over the 50-year period using today's technologies as a type of <a href="/wiki/Global_warming_game" title="Global warming game">Global warming game</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>Another consideration is how future <a href="/wiki/Socioeconomic_development" title="Socioeconomic development">socio-economic development</a> proceeds. Development choices (or "pathways") can lead differences in GHG emissions.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Political and social attitudes may affect how easy or difficult it is to implement effective policies to reduce emissions.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternative_energy_sources">Alternative energy sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_mitigation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Alternative energy sources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Renewable_energy">Renewable energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_mitigation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Renewable energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">Renewable energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_commercialization" title="Renewable energy commercialization">Renewable energy commercialization</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_debate" title="Renewable energy debate">Renewable energy debate</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bp_world_energy_consumption_2016.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Bp_world_energy_consumption_2016.gif/220px-Bp_world_energy_consumption_2016.gif" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Bp_world_energy_consumption_2016.gif/330px-Bp_world_energy_consumption_2016.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Bp_world_energy_consumption_2016.gif/440px-Bp_world_energy_consumption_2016.gif 2x" data-file-width="482" data-file-height="290" /></a>

The worldwide growth of renewable energy is shown by the green line<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ThreeGorgesDam-China2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/ThreeGorgesDam-China2009.jpg/220px-ThreeGorgesDam-China2009.jpg" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/ThreeGorgesDam-China2009.jpg/330px-ThreeGorgesDam-China2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/ThreeGorgesDam-China2009.jpg/440px-ThreeGorgesDam-China2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2847" data-file-height="1768" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shepherds_Flat_Wind_Farm_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Shepherds_Flat_Wind_Farm_2011.jpg/220px-Shepherds_Flat_Wind_Farm_2011.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Shepherds_Flat_Wind_Farm_2011.jpg/330px-Shepherds_Flat_Wind_Farm_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Shepherds_Flat_Wind_Farm_2011.jpg/440px-Shepherds_Flat_Wind_Farm_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2693" data-file-height="1801" /></a>

The <a href="/wiki/Shepherds_Flat_Wind_Farm" title="Shepherds Flat Wind Farm">Shepherds Flat Wind Farm</a> is an 845 <a href="/wiki/Megawatt" class="mw-redirect" title="Megawatt">megawatt</a> (MW) <a href="/wiki/Nameplate_capacity" title="Nameplate capacity">nameplate capacity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wind_farm" title="Wind farm">wind farm</a> in the U.S. state of <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a>, each turbine is a nameplate 2 or 2.5 MW electricity generator.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:12-05-08_AS1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/12-05-08_AS1.JPG/220px-12-05-08_AS1.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/12-05-08_AS1.JPG/330px-12-05-08_AS1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/12-05-08_AS1.JPG/440px-12-05-08_AS1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3504" data-file-height="2336" /></a>

The 150 MW <a href="/wiki/Andasol_solar_power_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Andasol solar power station">Andasol solar power station</a> is a commercial <a href="/wiki/Parabolic_trough" title="Parabolic trough">parabolic trough</a> <a href="/wiki/Solar_thermal" class="mw-redirect" title="Solar thermal">solar thermal</a> power plant, located in <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_in_Spain" title="Renewable energy in Spain">Spain</a>. The Andasol plant uses tanks of molten salt to store solar energy so that it can continue generating electricity for 7.5 hours after the sun has stopped shining.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Solar-Panel-Cooker-in-front-of-hut.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Solar-Panel-Cooker-in-front-of-hut.jpg/220px-Solar-Panel-Cooker-in-front-of-hut.jpg" width="220" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/25/Solar-Panel-Cooker-in-front-of-hut.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="322" data-file-height="285" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Solar-Panel-Cooker-in-front-of-hut.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Solar_cooker" title="Solar cooker">Solar cookers</a> use sunlight as energy source for outdoor cooking.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Renewable energy flows involve natural phenomena such as <a href="/wiki/Sunlight" title="Sunlight">sunlight</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wind" title="Wind">wind</a>, rain, <a href="/wiki/Tide" title="Tide">tides</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biomass" title="Biomass">plant growth</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_heating" title="Geothermal heating">geothermal heat</a>, as the <a href="/wiki/International_Energy_Agency" title="International Energy Agency">International Energy Agency</a> explains:<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Renewable energy is derived from natural processes that are replenished constantly. In its various forms, it derives directly from the sun, or from heat generated deep within the earth. Included in the definition is electricity and heat generated from solar, wind, ocean, <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydropower</a>, biomass, geothermal resources, and biofuels and hydrogen derived from renewable resources.</p>
</blockquote>
<p><a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">Climate change concerns</a><sup id="cite_ref-Stern_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stern-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ieapress_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ieapress-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UNEP2_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNEP2-55">[55]</a></sup> and the need to reduce carbon emissions are driving increasing growth in the <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Renewable energy industry">renewable energy industries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UNnews_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNnews-56">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mak_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mak-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UNEP_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNEP-58">[58]</a></sup> Low-carbon renewable energy replaces conventional fossil fuels in three main areas: <a href="/wiki/Power_generation" class="mw-redirect" title="Power generation">power generation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solar_hot_water" class="mw-redirect" title="Solar hot water">hot water</a>/ <a href="/wiki/Space_heating" class="mw-redirect" title="Space heating">space heating</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Transport_fuel" class="mw-redirect" title="Transport fuel">transport fuels</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ren15_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ren15-59">[59]</a></sup> In 2011, the share of renewables in <a href="/wiki/Electricity_generation" title="Electricity generation">electricity generation</a> worldwide grew for the fourth year in a row to 20.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Based on <a href="/wiki/REN21" title="REN21">REN21</a>'s 2014 report, renewables contributed 19% to supply global energy consumption. This energy consumption is divided as 9% coming from burning biomass, 4.2% as heat energy (non-biomass), 3.8% hydro electricity and 2% as electricity from wind, solar, geothermal, and biomass thermal power plants.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_commercialization" title="Renewable energy commercialization">Renewable energy use</a> has grown much faster than anyone anticipated.<sup id="cite_ref-pg11_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pg11-62">[62]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change</a> (IPCC) has said that there are few fundamental technological limits to integrating a portfolio of renewable energy technologies to meet most of total global energy demand.<sup id="cite_ref-IPCC_2011_17_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPCC_2011_17-63">[63]</a></sup> At the national level, at least 30 nations around the world already have renewable energy contributing more than 20% of energy supply.</p>
<p>As of 2012, renewable energy accounts for almost half of new electricity capacity installed and costs are continuing to fall.<sup id="cite_ref-irena111_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irena111-64">[64]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Public_policy" title="Public policy">Public policy</a> and political leadership helps to "level the playing field" and drive the wider acceptance of renewable energy technologies.<sup id="cite_ref-renewableenergyfocus.com_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-renewableenergyfocus.com-65">[65]</a></sup> As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_mitigation&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 118 countries have targets for their own renewable energy futures, and have enacted wide-ranging <a href="/wiki/Public_policies" class="mw-redirect" title="Public policies">public policies</a> to promote renewables.<sup id="cite_ref-map.ren21.net_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-map.ren21.net-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ren212011_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ren212011-67">[67]</a></sup> Leading renewable energy companies include <a href="/wiki/BrightSource_Energy" title="BrightSource Energy">BrightSource Energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/First_Solar" title="First Solar">First Solar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gamesa_Corporaci%C3%B3n_Tecnol%C3%B3gica" title="Gamesa Corporación Tecnológica">Gamesa</a>, <a href="/wiki/GE_Energy" title="GE Energy">GE Energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goldwind" title="Goldwind">Goldwind</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sinovel" title="Sinovel">Sinovel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suntech" class="mw-redirect" title="Suntech">Suntech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trina_Solar" title="Trina Solar">Trina Solar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vestas" title="Vestas">Vestas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yingli" title="Yingli">Yingli</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-top_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-top-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-keith_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-keith-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>The incentive to use <a href="/wiki/100%25_renewable_energy" title="100% renewable energy">100% renewable energy</a> has been created by <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> and other ecological as well as economic concerns.<sup id="cite_ref-pg11_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pg11-62">[62]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mark_Z._Jacobson" title="Mark Z. Jacobson">Mark Z. Jacobson</a> says producing all new energy with <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind power</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar power</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydropower</a> by 2030 is feasible and existing energy supply arrangements could be replaced by 2050. Barriers to implementing the renewable energy plan are seen to be "primarily social and political, not technological or economic". Jacobson says that energy costs with a wind, solar, water system should be similar to today's energy costs.<sup id="cite_ref-enpol2011_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-enpol2011-70">[70]</a></sup> According to a 2011 projection by the (IEA)<a href="/wiki/International_Energy_Agency" title="International Energy Agency">International Energy Agency</a>, solar power generators may produce most of the world's electricity within 50 years, dramatically reducing harmful greenhouse gas emissions.<sup id="cite_ref-ieaiea2011_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ieaiea2011-71">[71]</a></sup> Critics of the "100% renewable energy" approach include <a href="/wiki/Vaclav_Smil" title="Vaclav Smil">Vaclav Smil</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_E._Hansen" class="mw-redirect" title="James E. Hansen">James E. Hansen</a>. Smil and Hansen are concerned about the <a href="/wiki/Variable_renewable_energy" title="Variable renewable energy">variable output</a> of solar and wind power, <a href="/wiki/NIMBY" title="NIMBY">NIMBYism</a>, and a lack of infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>Economic analysts expect market gains for <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> (and <a href="/wiki/Efficient_energy_use" title="Efficient energy use">efficient energy use</a>) following the <a href="/wiki/2011_Japanese_nuclear_accidents" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Japanese nuclear accidents">2011 Japanese nuclear accidents</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> In his 2012 <a href="/wiki/State_of_the_Union" title="State of the Union">State of the Union</a> address, President Barack Obama restated his commitment to renewable energy and mentioned the long-standing Interior Department commitment to permit 10,000 MW of renewable energy projects on public land in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Lindsay_Morris_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lindsay_Morris-75">[75]</a></sup> Globally, there are an estimated 3 million direct jobs in renewable energy industries, with about half of them in the biofuels industry.<sup id="cite_ref-ren9_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ren9-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some countries, with favorable <a href="/wiki/Geography" title="Geography">geography</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geology" title="Geology">geology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Weather" title="Weather">weather</a> well suited to an economical exploitation of renewable energy sources, already get most of their electricity from renewables, including from <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_energy" title="Geothermal energy">geothermal energy</a> in Iceland (100 percent), and <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectric" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydroelectric">Hydroelectric</a> power in Brazil (85 percent), Austria (62 percent), New Zealand (65 percent), and Sweden (54 percent).<sup id="cite_ref-ren53_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ren53-77">[77]</a></sup> Renewable power generators are spread across many countries, with wind power providing a significant share of electricity in some regional areas: for example, 14 percent in the U.S. state of Iowa, 40 percent in the northern German state of Schleswig-Holstein, and 20 percent in Denmark. <a href="/wiki/Solar_water_heating" title="Solar water heating">Solar water heating</a> makes an important and growing contribution in many countries, most notably in China, which now has 70 percent of the global total (180 GWth). Worldwide, total installed solar water heating systems meet a portion of the water heating needs of over 70 million households. The use of <a href="/wiki/Biomass" title="Biomass">biomass</a> for heating continues to grow as well. In Sweden, national use of biomass energy has surpassed that of oil. Direct <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_heating" title="Geothermal heating">geothermal heating</a> is also growing rapidly.<sup id="cite_ref-ren53_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ren53-77">[77]</a></sup> Renewable <a href="/wiki/Biofuel" title="Biofuel">biofuels</a> for transportation, such as <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel" title="Ethanol fuel">ethanol fuel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biodiesel" title="Biodiesel">biodiesel</a>, have contributed to a significant decline in oil consumption in the United States since 2006. The 93&#160;billion liters of biofuels produced worldwide in 2009 displaced the equivalent of an estimated 68&#160;billion liters of gasoline, equal to about 5 percent of world gasoline production.<sup id="cite_ref-ren53_77-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ren53-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tnone center">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:458px;max-width:458px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:227px;max-width:227px">

</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:227px;max-width:227px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Topaz_Solar_Farm,_California_Valley.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Topaz_Solar_Farm%2C_California_Valley.jpg/225px-Topaz_Solar_Farm%2C_California_Valley.jpg" width="225" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Topaz_Solar_Farm%2C_California_Valley.jpg/338px-Topaz_Solar_Farm%2C_California_Valley.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Topaz_Solar_Farm%2C_California_Valley.jpg/450px-Topaz_Solar_Farm%2C_California_Valley.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="480" /></a></div>
