<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_divestment" title="Fossil fuel divestment">Fossil fuel divestment</a></div>
<p>Climate change is also a concern for large institutional investors who have a long term time horizon and potentially large exposure to the negative impacts of global warming because of the large geographic footprint of their multi-national holdings. SRI (<a href="/wiki/Socially_responsible_investing" title="Socially responsible investing">Socially responsible investing</a>) Funds allow investors to invest in funds that meet high ESG (environmental, social, governance) standards as such funds invest in companies that are aligned with these goals.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">[292]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Proxy_firm" title="Proxy firm">Proxy firms</a> can be used to draft guidelines for <a href="/wiki/Investment_manager" class="mw-redirect" title="Investment manager">investment managers</a> that take these concerns into account.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">[293]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_action">Legal action</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_mitigation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Legal action">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Duty_to_rescue" title="Duty to rescue">Duty to rescue</a></div>
<p>In some countries, those affected by climate change may be able to sue major producers. Attempts at litigation have been initiated by entire peoples such as Palau<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup> and the Inuit,<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[295]</a></sup> as well as non-governmental organizations such as the Sierra Club.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">[296]</a></sup> Although proving that particular weather events are due specifically to global warming may never be possible,<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">[297]</a></sup> methodologies have been developed to show the increased risk of such events caused by global warming.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">[298]</a></sup></p>
<p>For a legal action for <a href="/wiki/Negligence" title="Negligence">negligence</a> (or similar) to succeed, "Plaintiffs ... must show that, more probably than not, their individual injuries were caused by the risk factor in question, as opposed to any other cause. This has sometimes been translated to a requirement of a relative risk of at least two."<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">[299]</a></sup> Another route (though with little legal bite) is the <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Convention" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Convention">World Heritage Convention</a>, if it can be shown that climate change is affecting <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a> like <a href="/wiki/Mount_Everest" title="Mount Everest">Mount Everest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">[300]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">[301]</a></sup></p>
<p>Besides countries suing one another, there are also cases where people in a country have taken legal steps against their own government. Legal action for instance has been taken to try to force the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">U.S. Environmental Protection Agency</a> to regulate greenhouse gas emissions under the <a href="/wiki/Clean_Air_Act_(United_States)" title="Clean Air Act (United States)">Clean Air Act</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">[302]</a></sup> and against the <a href="/wiki/Export-Import_Bank_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Export-Import Bank of the United States">Export-Import Bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Private_Investment_Corporation" title="Overseas Private Investment Corporation">OPIC</a> for failing to assess environmental impacts (including global warming impacts) under <a href="/wiki/NEPA" class="mw-redirect" title="NEPA">NEPA</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In the Netherlands and Belgium, organisations as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Urgenda&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Urgenda (page does not exist)">Urgenda</a><sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">[303]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">[305]</a></sup> and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vzw_Klimaatzaak&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Vzw Klimaatzaak (page does not exist)">vzw Klimaatzaak</a> in Belgium<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">[306]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">[307]</a></sup> have also sued their governments as they believe their governments aren't meeting the emission reductions they agreed to. Urgenda has all ready won their case against the Dutch government.</p>
<p>According to a 2004 study commissioned by <a href="/wiki/Friends_of_the_Earth" title="Friends of the Earth">Friends of the Earth</a>, <a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil" title="ExxonMobil">ExxonMobil</a> and its predecessors caused 4.7 to 5.3 percent of the world's man-made carbon dioxide emissions between 1882 and 2002. The group suggested that such studies could form the basis for eventual legal action.<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">[308]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, <a href="/wiki/Exxon" title="Exxon">Exxon</a>, received a subpoena. According to the Washington Post and confirmed by the company, the attorney general of New York, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Schneiderman" title="Eric Schneiderman">Eric Schneiderman</a>, opened an investigation into the possibility that the company had mislead the public and investors about the risks of climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">[309]</a></sup></p>

Mark Lynas 2011</a></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-92"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-92">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.world-nuclear.org/information-library/nuclear-fuel-cycle/nuclear-wastes/radioactive-waste-management.aspx">"Radioactive Waste Management – Nuclear Waste Disposal"</a>. World Nuclear Association. 2016. <q>A typical 1000 MWe light water reactor will generate (directly and indirectly) 200–350 m3 low- and intermediate-level waste per year. It will also discharge about 20 m3 (27 tonnes) of used fuel per year, which corresponds to a 75 m3 disposal volume following encapsulation if it is treated as waste. Where that used fuel is reprocessed, only 3 m3 of vitrified waste (glass) is produced, which is equivalent to a 28 m3 disposal volume following placement in a disposal canister.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AClimate+change+mitigation&amp;rft.btitle=Radioactive+Waste+Management+%93+Nuclear+Waste+Disposal&amp;rft.date=2016&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.world-nuclear.org%2Finformation-library%2Fnuclear-fuel-cycle%2Fnuclear-wastes%2Fradioactive-waste-management.aspx&amp;rft.pub=World+Nuclear+Association&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>

<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>'s <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://ec.europa.eu/environment/climat/eccp.htm">European Climate Change Programme</a></li>

<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.hm-treasury.gov.uk/independent_reviews/stern_review_economics_climate_change/sternreview_index.cfm">The Stern Review on the economics of climate change</a> – Parts III and IV of the Stern Review are on climate change mitigation</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="US">US</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_mitigation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=65" title="Edit section: US">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.epa.gov/climatechange/wycd/index.html">EPA: What You Can Do</a>.</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.seattle.gov/mayor/climate/">U.S. Mayors Climate Protection Agreement</a> signed by 178 mayors representing nearly 40&#160;million Americans</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.climatechange.ca.gov/">California Climate Change Portal</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Academic">Academic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_mitigation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: Academic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Rivington M, Matthews KB, Buchan K and Miller D (2005) <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.macaulay.ac.uk/LADSS/papers.html?2005">"An integrated assessment approach to investigate options for mitigation and adaptation to climate change at the farm-scale"</a>, NJF Seminar 380, <a href="/wiki/Odense" title="Odense">Odense</a>, Denmark, 7–8 November 2005.</li>
<li><cite class="citation journal">Jacobson, M.Z.; Delucchi, M.A. (2009). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.scientificamerican.com/article.cfm?id=a-path-to-sustainable-energy-by-2030">"A Plan to Power 100 Percent of the Planet with Renewables" (originally published as "A Path to Sustainable Energy by 2030")"</a>. <i>Scientific American</i>. <b>301</b> (5): 58–65. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//dx.doi.org/10.1038%2Fscientificamerican1109-58">10.1038/scientificamerican1109-58</a>. <a href="/wiki/PubMed_Identifier" class="mw-redirect" title="PubMed Identifier">PMID</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19873905">19873905</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AClimate+change+mitigation&amp;rft.atitle=A+Plan+to+Power+100+Percent+of+the+Planet+with+Renewables%22+%28originally+published+as+%22A+Path+to+Sustainable+Energy+by+2030%22%29&amp;rft.au=Delucchi%2C+M.A.&amp;rft.aufirst=M.Z.&amp;rft.aulast=Jacobson&amp;rft.date=2009&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.scientificamerican.com%2Farticle.cfm%3Fid%3Da-path-to-sustainable-energy-by-2030&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1038%2Fscientificamerican1109-58&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F19873905&amp;rft.issue=5&amp;rft.jtitle=Scientific+American&amp;rft.pages=58-65&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.volume=301" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.scientificamerican.com/article.cfm?id=living-on-a-new-earth">Living On a New Earth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scientific_American" title="Scientific American">Scientific American</a> April 2010</li>

</ul>
